{
  "content": "# Cilium eBPF Map API Reference\n\n## Overview\n\nThe eBPF map API provides Go wrappers for user-space interaction with kernel eBPF maps. These maps serve as the primary data structure for sharing information between eBPF programs running in the kernel and user-space applications. This documentation covers the complete API contracts and behavioral semantics needed to effectively use eBPF maps in Cilium.\n\n---\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Core Map Types and Creation](#core-map-types-and-creation)\n2. [CRUD Operations](#crud-operations)\n3. [Iteration and Dumping](#iteration-and-dumping)\n4. [Pinning and Persistence](#pinning-and-persistence)\n5. [Key/Value Interfaces](#keyvalue-interfaces)\n6. [Event System](#event-system)\n7. [Collection Loading](#collection-loading)\n8. [Metrics and Monitoring](#metrics-and-monitoring)\n\n---\n\n## Core Map Types and Creation\n\n### Map Type\n\nThe `Map` struct represents an eBPF map and is the primary interface for map operations.\n\n```go\ntype Map struct {\n    Logger *slog.Logger  // Logger for debug/error output\n    // ... (additional unexported fields for internal state management)\n}\n```\n\n#### Key Methods\n\n**Type() ebpf.MapType**\n- Returns the map type (Hash, LRUHash, Array, PerCPUHash, etc.)\n- Returns `UnspecifiedMap` if the map has not been created yet\n\n**KeySize() uint32**\n- Returns the size in bytes of keys for this map\n\n**ValueSize() uint32**\n- Returns the size in bytes of values for this map\n\n**MaxEntries() uint32**\n- Returns the maximum number of entries the map can hold\n\n**Flags() uint32**\n- Returns the map flags\n\n**FD() int**\n- Returns the file descriptor of the underlying eBPF map\n- Only valid after the map has been opened/created\n\n### Map Creation Functions\n\n#### NewMap()\n\n```go\nfunc NewMap(name string, mapType ebpf.MapType, mapKey MapKey, mapValue MapValue,\n    maxEntries int, flags uint32) *Map\n```\n\nCreates a new Map instance for an eBPF map.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `name`: Map name (basename only, e.g., \"cilium_endpoints\")\n- `mapType`: Type of map (Hash, LRUHash, Array, etc.)\n- `mapKey`: Example key instance implementing MapKey interface\n- `mapValue`: Example value instance implementing MapValue interface\n- `maxEntries`: Maximum number of entries the map can hold\n- `flags`: BPF map creation flags\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Initializes a Map struct with a MapSpec but does not create the map in the kernel\n- The actual map is created when `Open()`, `OpenOrCreate()`, or `Create()` is called\n- The MapSpec is consumed (cleared) after the map is created in the kernel\n\n#### NewMapWithInnerSpec()\n\n```go\nfunc NewMapWithInnerSpec(name string, mapType ebpf.MapType, mapKey MapKey, mapValue MapValue,\n    maxEntries int, flags uint32, innerSpec *ebpf.MapSpec) *Map\n```\n\nCreates a new Map instance with an inner map specification, used for maps-of-maps.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- Same as NewMap, plus:\n- `innerSpec`: Map specification for the inner map (used with map-of-maps types)\n\n#### OpenMap()\n\n```go\nfunc OpenMap(pinPath string, key MapKey, value MapValue) (*Map, error)\n```\n\nOpens an existing pinned eBPF map from the filesystem.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `pinPath`: Absolute path to the pinned map\n- `key`: Example key instance implementing MapKey interface\n- `value`: Example value instance implementing MapValue interface\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Pins must be absolute paths (will return error if not)\n- The map must already exist at the specified path\n- The map is opened and ready for CRUD operations immediately\n- Returns error if the map cannot be found or accessed\n\n**Returns:**\n- `*Map`: An open map ready for operations\n- `error`: Non-nil if the map cannot be opened\n\n### Map Lifecycle Operations\n\n#### Open()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Open() error\n```\n\nOpens a pinned map for use. If the map is already open, this is a no-op.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Acquires the internal write lock\n- Looks for the map at its expected pinned path\n- Safe to call multiple times (idempotent)\n- Required before any CRUD operations if the map is not already open\n\n**Returns:**\n- `error`: Non-nil if the map cannot be found or opened\n\n#### OpenOrCreate()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) OpenOrCreate() error\n```\n\nAttempts to open the map, or creates it if it doesn't exist. If an existing map has incompatible attributes, it will be deleted and recreated without preserving contents.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- If the map file doesn't exist, creates it fresh\n- If the map file exists and is compatible (same type, key/value sizes, capacity), opens it and retains existing data\n- If the map file exists but is incompatible (different type, size, or capacity), deletes it and creates a new one\n- Maps created with this method are pinned to the filesystem\n- Non-persistent maps (marked appropriately) are always recreated\n- Acquires the internal write lock\n\n**Returns:**\n- `error`: Non-nil on creation/opening failure\n\n#### CreateUnpinned()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) CreateUnpinned() error\n```\n\nCreates the map in the kernel without pinning it to the filesystem.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Creates the map in kernel memory only\n- The map will not persist after the process exits\n- Useful for temporary maps or maps that shouldn't be shared across restarts\n- Acquires the internal write lock\n\n**Returns:**\n- `error`: Non-nil on creation failure\n\n#### Create()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Create() error\n```\n\nSimilar to `OpenOrCreate()`, but closes the map immediately after creation/opening.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Calls `OpenOrCreate()` to create or open the map\n- Immediately calls `Close()` to release the file descriptor\n- Useful when you only need to create/verify a map exists without keeping it open\n- The map remains pinned on the filesystem and can be opened later\n\n**Returns:**\n- `error`: Non-nil on creation failure\n\n#### Recreate()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Recreate() error\n```\n\nRemoves any pin at the map's path, then recreates and re-pins the map.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Removes the existing pinned map file\n- Recreates the map in the kernel\n- Re-pins the new map to the filesystem\n- Deletes all previous map contents\n- Acquires the internal write lock\n\n**Returns:**\n- `error`: Non-nil if the map is already open, or if recreation fails\n\n#### IsOpen()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) IsOpen() bool\n```\n\nReturns true if the map has been opened and is ready for operations.\n\n#### Close()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Close() error\n```\n\nCloses the map and releases the file descriptor.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Closes the underlying eBPF map\n- Stops any running error resolver controller\n- Unregisters the map from internal tracking\n- Does not remove the map from the filesystem (map remains pinned)\n- Safe to call multiple times (idempotent)\n\n**Returns:**\n- `error`: Non-nil on close failure (rare)\n\n---\n\n## CRUD Operations\n\n### Lookup\n\n#### Lookup()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Lookup(key MapKey) (MapValue, error)\n```\n\nRetrieves the value associated with a key from the map.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Opens the map if not already open\n- Acquires a read lock for the duration of the lookup\n- Returns a new instance of the value type\n- Returns `nil, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist` if the key is not in the map\n- Tracks syscall metrics if enabled\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `key`: The key to look up (must implement MapKey)\n\n**Returns:**\n- `MapValue`: A new instance containing the value, or nil if not found\n- `error`: `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist` if key not found, or other errors\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nkey := &MyKey{ID: 123}\nvalue, err := myMap.Lookup(key)\nif err != nil {\n    if errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\n        // Key not in map\n    } else {\n        // Other error occurred\n    }\n}\n// Use value\n```\n\n### Update\n\n#### Update()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Update(key MapKey, value MapValue) error\n```\n\nInserts or updates a key-value pair in the map.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Opens the map if not already open\n- Acquires a write lock\n- Creates the entry if it doesn't exist, or replaces it if it does\n- If cache is enabled, updates the cache entry with status OK on success\n- If cache is enabled and update fails, marks the entry for error recovery\n- Triggers error resolver scheduling on failure if cache is enabled\n- Records the update in the event buffer if events are enabled\n- Tracks operation metrics\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `key`: The key to update (must implement MapKey)\n- `value`: The new value (must implement MapValue)\n\n**Returns:**\n- `error`: Non-nil on update failure\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nkey := &MyKey{ID: 123}\nvalue := &MyValue{Data: 42}\nif err := myMap.Update(key, value); err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"Failed to update: %v\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### Delete\n\n#### Delete()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Delete(key MapKey) error\n```\n\nDeletes a key-value pair from the map.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Opens the map if not already open\n- Acquires a write lock\n- Returns error if the key doesn't exist\n- If cache is enabled, removes the entry from the cache on success\n- If cache is enabled and delete fails, marks the entry with error status\n- Records the deletion in the event buffer\n- Triggers error resolver scheduling on failure if cache is enabled\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `key`: The key to delete (must implement MapKey)\n\n**Returns:**\n- `error`: `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist` if key not found, or other errors\n\n#### SilentDelete()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) SilentDelete(key MapKey) (deleted bool, error)\n```\n\nDeletes a key-value pair, ignoring errors if the key doesn't exist.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Same as Delete() but returns `(false, nil)` instead of an error if the key is not found\n- Useful for cleanup operations where missing keys are acceptable\n- Still records in event buffer and cache\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `key`: The key to delete\n\n**Returns:**\n- `deleted`: True if the key was found and deleted\n- `error`: Non-nil only for errors other than missing key\n\n#### DeleteLocked()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DeleteLocked(key MapKey) error\n```\n\nDeletes a key-value pair from within a DumpCallback without deadlock.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Must only be called from within a DumpCallback function\n- Assumes the map lock is already acquired (by DumpReliablyWithCallback)\n- Does not acquire the lock itself, avoiding deadlock when called from a callback\n- Otherwise behaves like Delete()\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `key`: The key to delete\n\n**Returns:**\n- `error`: Non-nil on deletion failure\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nmyMap.DumpReliablyWithCallback(func(key, value any) {\n    // Safe to delete here\n    if shouldDelete(key) {\n        if err := myMap.DeleteLocked(key); err != nil {\n            log.Printf(\"Delete failed: %v\", err)\n        }\n    }\n}, stats)\n```\n\n#### DeleteAll()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DeleteAll() error\n```\n\nDeletes all entries from the map by iterating and deleting individually.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Opens the map if not already open\n- Acquires a write lock for the entire operation\n- Iterates over all entries and deletes each one\n- If cache is enabled, marks all entries for deletion before starting\n- Records successful deletions by removing cache entries\n- Records failed deletions by marking cache entries with error status\n- Note: Entries added while deletion is in progress may not be deleted\n- Updates pressure metrics after completion\n\n**Returns:**\n- `error`: Non-nil if iteration or deletion fails\n\n#### ClearAll()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) ClearAll() error\n```\n\nClears all entries by setting them to empty values instead of deleting.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Only works for maps without value cache or events buffer enabled\n- Returns error if either feature is enabled\n- Iterates over all entries and updates each to an empty/zero value\n- Faster than DeleteAll for some use cases\n- Does not record in event buffer (not allowed if events are enabled)\n\n**Returns:**\n- `error`: Non-nil if cache/events enabled or if operation fails\n\n### NextKey\n\n#### NextKey()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) NextKey(key, nextKeyOut any) error\n```\n\nGets the next key in iteration order after the given key.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Acquires a read lock\n- If key is nil, returns the first key in the map\n- Returns `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist` when iteration completes\n- Used for iterating maps without fetching values\n- Lower-level interface; prefer DumpWithCallback for easier iteration\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `key`: Current key (nil to get first)\n- `nextKeyOut`: Pointer to where next key will be written\n\n**Returns:**\n- `error`: `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist` at end of iteration, or other errors\n\n---\n\n## Iteration and Dumping\n\n### DumpWithCallback\n\n#### DumpWithCallback()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpWithCallback(cb DumpCallback) error\n```\n\nIterates over all map entries and calls a callback for each.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `cb`: Function called for each entry with signature `func(key, value MapKey)`\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Opens the map if not already open\n- Acquires a read lock for the entire iteration\n- Invokes the callback once for each entry with fresh key and value instances\n- Does not hold the lock during callback execution (released for each iteration)\n- Callback receives new instances, safe to retain values\n- Used for simple one-time reads of all map contents\n- Returns error if callback is nil\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nresults := make(map[string]string)\nerr := myMap.DumpWithCallback(func(key, value MapKey) {\n    results[key.String()] = value.String()\n})\n```\n\n#### DumpPerCPUWithCallback()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpPerCPUWithCallback(cb DumpPerCPUCallback) error\n```\n\nIterates over per-CPU map entries, calling a callback with values from all CPUs.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `cb`: Function with signature `func(key MapKey, values any)`\n  - `values` is a slice of per-CPU values, one per CPU\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Only works with per-CPU map types (PerCPUHash, PerCPUArray, LRUCPUHash, PerCPUCGroupStorage)\n- The map's value type must implement MapPerCPUValue (has NewSlice() method)\n- Acquires a read lock\n- Calls callback for each unique key with a slice of values from all CPUs\n- Callback receives new instances, safe to retain\n\n**Returns:**\n- `error`: Non-nil if map is not per-CPU, value type incompatible, or iteration fails\n\n#### DumpWithCallbackIfExists()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpWithCallbackIfExists(cb DumpCallback) error\n```\n\nLike DumpWithCallback, but returns earlier if the map doesn't exist.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Checks if the map exists on the filesystem first\n- If it doesn't exist, returns nil immediately without calling the callback\n- If it exists, proceeds with normal DumpWithCallback operation\n- Useful for optional maps that may not always exist\n\n#### DumpReliablyWithCallback()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb DumpCallback, stats *DumpStats) error\n```\n\nIterates over all map entries with recovery from concurrent modifications.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Designed for maps that may be modified concurrently during iteration\n- Acquires a write lock for the entire operation\n- Tracks recently seen keys to recover from mid-iteration deletions\n- If a key is deleted during iteration, continues from the most recently seen key\n- Caps maximum iterations at 4x the map's MaxEntries to prevent infinite loops\n- Returns ErrMaxLookup if iteration limit is exceeded\n- Returns error if stats is nil or callback is nil\n- Callback must not acquire the Map.lock (lock is held for entire iteration)\n- **Important**: DeleteLocked() can be safely called from the callback\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `cb`: DumpCallback function\n- `stats`: Pointer to DumpStats initialized via NewDumpStats()\n\n**Returns:**\n- `error`: ErrMaxLookup if iteration limit exceeded, or other errors\n- The stats object is populated with iteration metrics\n\n**Statistics Available:**\n- `Lookup`: Number of NextKey calls performed\n- `LookupFailed`: Number of lookups that failed\n- `KeyFallback`: Times we fell back to previous key after deletion\n- `Interrupted`: Times iteration had to restart from scratch\n- `Completed`: True if iteration completed successfully\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nstats := NewDumpStats(myMap)\nerr := myMap.DumpReliablyWithCallback(func(key, value MapKey) {\n    // Safe to call myMap.DeleteLocked(key) here\n    process(key, value)\n}, stats)\n\nif err == ErrMaxLookup {\n    log.Printf(\"Iteration limit exceeded\")\n}\nlog.Printf(\"Looked up %d entries, completed: %v\", stats.Lookup, stats.Completed)\n```\n\n### Dump\n\n#### Dump()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Dump(hash map[string][]string) error\n```\n\nConvenience function that dumps all map entries into a map[string][]string.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Calls DumpWithCallback internally\n- Returns map keyed by string representation of keys\n- Values are slices of string representations (allows multiple values per key)\n- Creates strings from key.String() and value.String()\n- No deep copying needed (strings are created from key/value strings)\n\n**Returns:**\n- `error`: Non-nil on dump failure\n\n#### DumpIfExists()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpIfExists(hash map[string][]string) error\n```\n\nLike Dump, but returns nil if the map doesn't exist on the filesystem.\n\n### BatchIterator\n\n#### NewBatchIterator()\n\n```go\nfunc NewBatchIterator[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](m *Map) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n```\n\nCreates a new batch iterator for efficient iteration using the eBPF batch lookup API.\n\n**Generic Parameters:**\n- `KT`: Key type\n- `VT`: Value type\n- `KP`: Key pointer constraint (must be MapKey)\n- `VP`: Value pointer constraint (must be MapValue)\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Provides typed iteration interface\n- Supports automatic retry on ENOSPC errors (buffer too small)\n- More efficient than traditional iteration for large maps\n- Automatically handles batch sizing\n\n**Example:**\n```go\ntype MyKey struct { ID uint32 }\ntype MyValue struct { Data uint64 }\n\n// Types must implement MapKey and MapValue interfaces\niter := NewBatchIterator[MyKey, MyValue](myMap)\nfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(context.Background()) {\n    process(*k, *v)\n}\nif err := iter.Err(); err != nil {\n    log.Printf(\"Iteration failed: %v\", err)\n}\n```\n\n#### IterateAll()\n\n```go\nfunc (bi *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) IterateAll(ctx context.Context,\n    opts ...BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]) iter.Seq2[KP, VP]\n```\n\nReturns a sequence for range-based iteration over all map entries.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Resets internal state on each call (reusable iterator)\n- Automatically handles ENOSPC errors by growing buffer (up to 3 retries by default)\n- Returns error via Err() if buffer grows too large or other errors occur\n- Respects context cancellation\n- Yields pointers to keys and values\n- Yields are references to internal buffers; copy if retaining values\n\n**Options (via functional parameters):**\n- `WithEBPFBatchOpts()`: Override BPF_MAP_LOOKUP_BATCH options\n- `WithMaxRetries()`: Change max retry count for ENOSPC (default 3)\n- `WithStartingChunkSize()`: Set initial batch size (default auto-calculated)\n\n**Returns:**\n- `iter.Seq2[KP, VP]`: Range-iterable sequence of key-value pointers\n\n#### Err()\n\n```go\nfunc (bi BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) Err() error\n```\n\nReturns any error encountered during the most recent IterateAll() call.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Cleared on each IterateAll() call\n- Returns nil if iteration completed successfully\n\n#### CountAll()\n\n```go\nfunc CountAll[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](\n    ctx context.Context, iter *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) (int, error)\n```\n\nConvenience helper that counts all entries in the map using a batch iterator.\n\n**Returns:**\n- `int`: Count of entries\n- `error`: Iteration error from iter.Err()\n\n### BatchLookup\n\n#### BatchLookup()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) BatchLookup(cursor *ebpf.MapBatchCursor, keysOut, valuesOut any,\n    opts *ebpf.BatchOptions) (int, error)\n```\n\nLower-level batch lookup interface for advanced iteration scenarios.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Direct wrapper around ebpf.Map.BatchLookup\n- Caller responsible for managing cursor and buffer sizes\n- More control but requires manual ENOSPC handling\n- Less convenient than BatchIterator for most use cases\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `cursor`: State maintained across calls for continued iteration\n- `keysOut`: Slice to receive keys\n- `valuesOut`: Slice to receive values\n- `opts`: Optional batch options\n\n**Returns:**\n- `int`: Number of entries returned\n- `error`: `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist` at end, `unix.ENOSPC` if buffer too small, or other errors\n\n#### BatchCount()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) BatchCount() (count int, err error)\n```\n\nCounts the total number of entries in the map using batch lookups.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Uses batch lookup with no-op decoders (doesn't store actual data)\n- Automatically retries and grows buffers on ENOSPC\n- Only works for Hash, LRUHash, and LPMTrie map types\n- More efficient than iterating all entries\n\n**Returns:**\n- `count`: Total number of entries\n- `error`: Non-nil if counting fails\n\n---\n\n## Pinning and Persistence\n\n### Pin and Unpin\n\n#### Pin() (implicit via OpenOrCreate)\n\nMaps are automatically pinned to the filesystem when created with `OpenOrCreate()`.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Pinned maps persist on disk after the process exits\n- Pinned maps can be opened by other processes\n- Pin path is derived from the map name using `MapPath()`\n- Automatically handled by `OpenOrCreate()` and `Create()`\n\n#### Unpin()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Unpin() error\n```\n\nRemoves the pin of the map from the filesystem.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Deletes the map file from the BPF filesystem\n- The map may still exist in kernel memory if other processes have it open\n- Safe to call even if the map is open\n\n**Returns:**\n- `error`: Non-nil if the pin cannot be removed\n\n#### UnpinIfExists()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) UnpinIfExists() error\n```\n\nRemoves the pin only if it exists on the filesystem.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Checks for existence first\n- Returns nil if the pin doesn't exist\n- Useful for cleanup that shouldn't fail if map was never pinned\n\n**Returns:**\n- `error`: Non-nil if removal fails (but nil if pin doesn't exist)\n\n### Path Management\n\n#### Path()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Path() (string, error)\n```\n\nReturns the filesystem path where the map is or will be pinned.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Automatically determines path if not already set\n- Sets path based on map name if needed\n- Returns error if path cannot be determined (no name or logger issues)\n\n**Returns:**\n- `string`: Absolute path to the map pin\n- `error`: Non-nil if path cannot be determined\n\n#### Name()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Name() string\n```\n\nReturns the basename (filename only) of the map.\n\n**Example:**\n```go\npath, _ := myMap.Path()           // \"/sys/fs/bpf/tc/globals/cilium_endpoints\"\nname := myMap.Name()               // \"cilium_endpoints\"\n```\n\n### Filesystem Functions\n\n#### BPFFSRoot()\n\n```go\nfunc BPFFSRoot() string\n```\n\nReturns the root mount point of the BPF filesystem.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns the configured BPF filesystem mount point (usually `/sys/fs/bpf`)\n- Locks in the value after first call (cannot be changed)\n\n#### CiliumPath()\n\n```go\nfunc CiliumPath() string\n```\n\nReturns the bpffs path for Cilium map pins.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns `<BPFFSRoot>/cilium`\n- Used for storing Cilium-specific map pins\n\n#### MapPath()\n\n```go\nfunc MapPath(logger *slog.Logger, name string) string\n```\n\nReturns the full filesystem path for a map with the given name.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- For Cilium agent: returns `<BPFFSRoot>/tc/globals/<name>`\n- For other components: may use other paths depending on context\n- Does not create directories\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `logger`: Logger for potential error messages\n- `name`: Map name (basename)\n\n#### MkdirBPF()\n\n```go\nfunc MkdirBPF(path string) error\n```\n\nCreates a directory on the BPF filesystem with correct permissions (755).\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Creates all parent directories as needed\n- Sets permissions to 0755\n\n#### CheckOrMountFS()\n\n```go\nfunc CheckOrMountFS(logger *slog.Logger, bpfRoot string)\n```\n\nChecks and mounts the BPF filesystem if needed.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Checks if BPF filesystem is mounted at the specified location\n- If not mounted and location is empty or default, attempts to mount\n- If mounted elsewhere, uses fallback locations\n- Exits with fatal error if BPF filesystem cannot be mounted\n- Only runs once per process (subsequent calls are no-ops)\n\n---\n\n## Key/Value Interfaces\n\n### MapKey Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapKey interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n\n    // New must return a pointer to a new MapKey of the same type.\n    New() MapKey\n}\n```\n\nCustom key types must implement this interface.\n\n**Requirements:**\n- Must implement `String()` for string representation\n- `New()` must return a pointer to a fresh instance of the same type\n- Must be a struct that can be marshaled as binary data by ebpf-go\n- All struct fields must be properly aligned (use `align:` tags if needed)\n- Field order must match the eBPF structure definition\n\n**Example:**\n```go\ntype MyKey struct {\n    ID   uint32\n    Flags uint8\n}\n\nfunc (k *MyKey) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"ID=%d,Flags=%d\", k.ID, k.Flags)\n}\n\nfunc (k *MyKey) New() MapKey {\n    return &MyKey{}\n}\n```\n\n### MapValue Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapValue interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n\n    // New must return a pointer to a new MapValue of the same type.\n    New() MapValue\n}\n```\n\nCustom value types must implement this interface.\n\n**Requirements:**\n- Must implement `String()` for string representation\n- `New()` must return a pointer to a fresh instance\n- Must be a struct that can be marshaled as binary data by ebpf-go\n- Supports the same alignment and structure requirements as MapKey\n\n### MapPerCPUValue Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapPerCPUValue interface {\n    MapValue\n\n    // NewSlice must return a pointer to a slice of structs that implement MapValue.\n    NewSlice() any\n}\n```\n\nValues in per-CPU maps must implement this interface.\n\n**Requirements:**\n- Must embed or implement MapValue\n- `NewSlice()` must return a pointer to a slice of the value type\n- One slice element per CPU in the system\n\n**Example:**\n```go\ntype PerCPUCounter struct {\n    Count uint64\n}\n\nfunc (c *PerCPUCounter) String() string { ... }\nfunc (c *PerCPUCounter) New() MapValue { return &PerCPUCounter{} }\n\nfunc (c *PerCPUCounter) NewSlice() any {\n    // Return slice with one element per CPU\n    numCPU := runtime.NumCPU()\n    slice := make([]PerCPUCounter, numCPU)\n    return &slice\n}\n```\n\n### EndpointKey Example\n\n```go\ntype EndpointKey struct {\n    IP        types.IPv6 `align:\"$union0\"`  // Stores both IPv6 and IPv4\n    Family    uint8      `align:\"family\"`\n    Key       uint8      `align:\"key\"`\n    ClusterID uint16     `align:\"cluster_id\"`\n}\n\nfunc (k EndpointKey) String() string { ... }\nfunc (k *EndpointKey) New() MapKey { return &EndpointKey{} }\n```\n\n---\n\n## Event System\n\n### Event Types\n\n#### Action Enum\n\n```go\nconst (\n    MapUpdate  Action = iota  // Entry was updated\n    MapDelete               // Entry was deleted\n    MapDeleteAll            // All entries deleted (aggregated event)\n)\n```\n\n### Event Structure\n\n```go\ntype Event struct {\n    Timestamp     time.Time      // When the event occurred\n    // GetAction() returns \"update\", \"delete\", or \"delete-all\"\n    // GetKey() returns string representation of the key\n    // GetValue() returns string representation of the value (or \"<nil>\")\n    // GetLastError() returns any error that occurred\n    // GetDesiredAction() returns the desired cache action\n}\n```\n\n### Enabling Events\n\n#### WithEvents()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithEvents(c option.BPFEventBufferConfig) *Map\n```\n\nEnables the event buffer for the map.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Stores recent map events (updates, deletes) in a bounded buffer\n- Returns the map for chaining\n- If events buffer is disabled in config, this is a no-op\n- Allocates approximately 100MB per million map capacity\n- Can be paired with DumpAndSubscribe for streaming events\n\n**Configuration:**\n```go\ntype BPFEventBufferConfig struct {\n    Enabled bool\n    MaxSize int\n    TTL     time.Duration  // How long to keep old events\n}\n```\n\n### DumpAndSubscribe\n\n#### DumpAndSubscribe()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpAndSubscribe(ctx context.Context, callback EventCallbackFunc, follow bool)\n```\n\nDumps existing events and optionally subscribes to new ones.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Acquires a read lock to safely dump events\n- Calls callback for each existing event in the buffer\n- If follow=true, subscribes to future events using the stream system\n- Events are delivered to the callback as they occur\n- Subscription is canceled when context is canceled\n- Dumps and subscription happen atomically (no events missed between them)\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `ctx`: Context for subscription (controls when subscription ends)\n- `callback`: Function called for each event (type: `func(Event)`)\n- `follow`: If true, subscribe to future events; if false, only dump existing\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())\ndefer cancel()\n\nmyMap.DumpAndSubscribe(ctx, func(event Event) {\n    log.Printf(\"%s: key=%s, value=%s, error=%v\",\n        event.GetAction(), event.GetKey(), event.GetValue(), event.GetLastError())\n}, true)  // Subscribe to future events\n```\n\n#### IsEventsEnabled()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) IsEventsEnabled() bool\n```\n\nReturns true if the event buffer is enabled for this map.\n\n---\n\n## Collection Loading\n\nCollections allow loading multiple eBPF maps and programs together with coordinated behavior.\n\n### CollectionOptions\n\n```go\ntype CollectionOptions struct {\n    ebpf.CollectionOptions\n\n    // Constants are runtime config replacements for DECLARE_CONFIG values\n    Constants any\n\n    // MapRenames allows renaming maps during loading\n    MapRenames []map[string]string\n\n    // MapReplacements passes inner maps for map-of-maps types\n    MapReplacements map[string]*Map\n\n    // Keep specifies objects to preserve during dead code elimination\n    Keep *set.Set[string]\n\n    // ConfigDumpPath writes runtime constants to a file\n    ConfigDumpPath string\n}\n```\n\n### LoadCollection()\n\n```go\nfunc LoadCollection(logger *slog.Logger, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec,\n    opts *CollectionOptions) (*ebpf.Collection, func() error, error)\n```\n\nLoads an eBPF collection (maps and programs) into the kernel.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Validates that all programs have specified types (no UnspecifiedProgram)\n- Applies map renames and constant overrides\n- Computes reachability and removes unreachable code\n- Resolves tail calls in program arrays\n- Handles CILIUM_PIN_REPLACE flags for map pinning\n- Detects incompatible existing maps and recreaates them\n- Returns a commit function that must be called after attaching programs\n- The commit function replaces old map pins with new ones\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `logger`: Logger for operation output\n- `spec`: eBPF collection specification\n- `opts`: Loading options (nil defaults to empty options)\n\n**Returns:**\n- `*ebpf.Collection`: Loaded maps and programs ready to attach\n- `func() error`: Commit function (call after program attachment)\n- `error`: Non-nil if loading fails\n\n**Workflow:**\n```go\n// Step 1: Load the collection\ncoll, commit, err := LoadCollection(logger, spec, opts)\nif err != nil {\n    return err\n}\ndefer coll.Close()\n\n// Step 2: Attach programs to kernel hooks (xdp, tc, etc.)\n// ... your attachment code ...\n\n// Step 3: Commit map pins after all programs attached\nif err := commit(); err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n```\n\n### LoadAndAssign()\n\n```go\nfunc LoadAndAssign(logger *slog.Logger, to any, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec,\n    opts *CollectionOptions) (func() error, error)\n```\n\nConvenience function combining LoadCollection with struct field assignment.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Calls LoadCollection to load the eBPF collection\n- Uses reflection to assign maps and programs to struct fields\n- Prints verifier errors to stderr if verification fails\n- Returns the commit function for deferred map pin operations\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `logger`: Logger for operation output\n- `to`: Struct with fields matching maps and programs in the collection\n- `spec`: eBPF collection specification\n- `opts`: Loading options\n\n**Returns:**\n- `func() error`: Commit function (call after program attachment)\n- `error`: Non-nil if loading or assignment fails\n\n**Example:**\n```go\ntype Objects struct {\n    Endpoints *ebpf.Map     `ebpf:\"cilium_endpoints\"`\n    Program   *ebpf.Program `ebpf:\"tc_egress\"`\n}\n\nobjs := &Objects{}\ncommit, err := LoadAndAssign(logger, objs, spec, &CollectionOptions{\n    Maps: ebpf.CollectionOptions{PinPath: \"/sys/fs/bpf/cilium\"},\n})\nif err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n// After attaching objs.Program...\ncommit()\n```\n\n---\n\n## Caching and Error Recovery\n\n### WithCache\n\n#### WithCache()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithCache() *Map\n```\n\nEnables local caching of map entries.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Maintains a local map[string]*cacheEntry tracking all user-space updates\n- Records desired action (Insert/Delete) and last error for each entry\n- Enables automatic error recovery via periodic reconciliation\n- Returns the map for method chaining\n- Incompatible with non-persistent maps\n\n**Cache Entry States:**\n- `OK`: Entry is in sync with kernel map\n- `Insert`: Entry needs to be inserted/updated in kernel\n- `Delete`: Entry needs to be deleted from kernel\n\n#### WithPressureMetric()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithPressureMetric(registry *metrics.Registry) *Map\n```\n\nEnables tracking of map utilization as a gauge metric.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Tracks cache size as a percentage of MaxEntries\n- Registers a metric with the provided registry\n- Returns the map for chaining\n- Only works if WithCache() is enabled\n- Useful for monitoring map capacity pressure\n\n#### WithPressureMetricThreshold()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithPressureMetricThreshold(registry *metrics.Registry, threshold float64) *Map\n```\n\nLike WithPressureMetric, but only reports the metric if utilization exceeds threshold.\n\n### Grouping\n\n#### WithGroupName()\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithGroupName(group string) *Map\n```\n\nSets the metric group name for this map.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Used for grouping metrics of related maps\n- All maps in the same group share metric aggregation\n- Useful for tracking total capacity across multiple map instances\n\n---\n\n## Configuration Builders (Fluent API)\n\nMap configuration methods support fluent chaining:\n\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"my_map\", ebpf.Hash, &MyKey{}, &MyValue{}, 1000, 0).\n    WithCache().\n    WithGroupName(\"my_group\").\n    WithPressureMetric(registry).\n    WithEvents(BPFEventBufferConfig{\n        Enabled: true,\n        MaxSize: 10000,\n        TTL:     time.Hour,\n    })\n\nif err := m.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Behavior Semantics\n\n### Map Lifecycle\n\n1. **Creation**: `NewMap()` creates a Map instance with MapSpec but no kernel map\n2. **Opening**: `Open()`, `OpenOrCreate()`, or `Create()` creates the kernel map\n3. **Operations**: CRUD operations open the map if needed\n4. **Closing**: `Close()` releases the file descriptor but keeps the pin\n5. **Cleanup**: `Unpin()` removes the filesystem pin\n\n### Create vs OpenOrCreate\n\n**Create()**: Creates or opens a map, then immediately closes the file descriptor\n- Useful for map initialization that's separate from usage\n- Validates that the map can be created/opened\n- The map remains pinned and can be opened later\n\n**OpenOrCreate()**: Creates or opens a map and keeps it open\n- Locks the map for subsequent operations\n- Used when you need continuous access to the map\n\n### Deletion Within Iteration\n\nWhen deleting entries during iteration:\n- Use `DeleteLocked()` inside `DumpReliablyWithCallback()` callbacks\n- Cannot delete during `DumpWithCallback()` (acquires only read lock)\n- Cannot delete outside callbacks (would deadlock if callback holds lock)\n\n### Error Recovery\n\nMaps with cache enabled can recover from transient errors:\n- Failed Update/Delete operations mark entries in cache with error state\n- A periodic error resolver (controller) scans the cache\n- Resolver retries failed operations up to `maxSyncErrors` per run\n- Resolved entries are marked as `OK` in the cache\n\n### Per-CPU Maps\n\nFor per-CPU maps:\n- Use `DumpPerCPUWithCallback()` instead of `DumpWithCallback()`\n- Value type must implement `MapPerCPUValue`\n- `NewSlice()` returns a slice with one element per CPU\n- Operations on per-CPU maps are automatically replicated across CPUs\n\n### Batch Iterator Retry Logic\n\nBatchIterator automatically handles buffer sizing:\n- Starts with buffer size based on sqrt(MaxEntries * 2)\n- Retries with 2x larger buffer on ENOSPC error (up to 3 times by default)\n- Suitable for LRU maps with variable bucket sizes\n- Non-LRU hash maps rarely hit ENOSPC\n\n---\n\n## Common Patterns\n\n### Safe Iteration with Deletions\n\n```go\nstats := NewDumpStats(myMap)\nerr := myMap.DumpReliablyWithCallback(func(key, value MapKey) {\n    if shouldDelete(key.(MapKey)) {\n        if err := myMap.DeleteLocked(key.(MapKey)); err != nil {\n            log.Printf(\"Delete failed: %v\", err)\n        }\n    } else {\n        process(key, value)\n    }\n}, stats)\n\nif err != nil {\n    log.Printf(\"Dump error: %v\", err)\n}\nlog.Printf(\"Iteration stats: %+v\", stats)\n```\n\n### Efficient Large Map Iteration\n\n```go\niter := NewBatchIterator[MyKey, MyValue](myMap)\ncount := 0\nfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(context.Background()) {\n    count++\n    process(*k, *v)\n}\nif err := iter.Err(); err != nil {\n    log.Printf(\"Iteration error: %v\", err)\n}\nlog.Printf(\"Processed %d entries\", count)\n```\n\n### Map with Event Monitoring\n\n```go\nmyMap := NewMap(\"events_map\", ebpf.Hash, &EventKey{}, &EventValue{}, 10000, 0).\n    WithCache().\n    WithEvents(BPFEventBufferConfig{\n        Enabled: true,\n        MaxSize: 1000,\n        TTL:     5 * time.Minute,\n    })\n\nif err := myMap.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n\nctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())\ndefer cancel()\n\n// Dump existing events and subscribe to new ones\nmyMap.DumpAndSubscribe(ctx, func(evt Event) {\n    log.Printf(\"Event: %s on key %s\", evt.GetAction(), evt.GetKey())\n}, true)\n```\n\n### Map-of-Maps\n\n```go\n// Create inner map spec\ninnerSpec := &ebpf.MapSpec{\n    Name:       \"inner_map\",\n    Type:       ebpf.Hash,\n    KeySize:    4,\n    ValueSize:  8,\n    MaxEntries: 100,\n}\n\n// Create outer map with inner spec\nouterMap := NewMapWithInnerSpec(\n    \"outer_map\",\n    ebpf.HashOfMaps,\n    &OuterKey{},\n    &OuterValue{},\n    1000,\n    0,\n    innerSpec,\n)\n\nif err := outerMap.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Important Notes\n\n- **Lock Safety**: All public methods handle locking internally. Calling code doesn't need to manage locks manually.\n- **Callback Constraints**: Callbacks should complete quickly; long-running callbacks block iteration.\n- **Memory Safety**: Returned values from Lookup are new instances; safe to retain.\n- **File Descriptor Lifetime**: After Close(), the file descriptor is invalid. The map remains pinned on the filesystem.\n- **Concurrency**: Multiple goroutines can safely call different methods on the same Map; lock-free reads are safe for Type(), KeySize(), ValueSize(), MaxEntries(), Flags().\n- **Pin Paths**: Maps created by the agent are pinned in `/sys/fs/bpf/tc/globals/`. Use MapPath() to determine the actual path.\n",

# Cilium eBPF Map API Reference

## Overview

The eBPF map API provides Go wrappers for user-space interaction with kernel eBPF maps. These maps serve as the primary data structure for sharing information between eBPF programs running in the kernel and user-space applications. This documentation covers the complete API contracts and behavioral semantics needed to effectively use eBPF maps in Cilium.

---

## Table of Contents

1. [Core Map Types and Creation](#core-map-types-and-creation)
2. [CRUD Operations](#crud-operations)
3. [Iteration and Dumping](#iteration-and-dumping)
4. [Pinning and Persistence](#pinning-and-persistence)
5. [Key/Value Interfaces](#keyvalue-interfaces)
6. [Event System](#event-system)
7. [Collection Loading](#collection-loading)
8. [Metrics and Monitoring](#metrics-and-monitoring)

---

## Core Map Types and Creation

### Map Type

The `Map` struct represents an eBPF map and is the primary interface for map operations.

```go
type Map struct {
    Logger *slog.Logger  // Logger for debug/error output
    // ... (additional unexported fields for internal state management)
}
```

#### Key Methods

**Type() ebpf.MapType**
- Returns the map type (Hash, LRUHash, Array, PerCPUHash, etc.)
- Returns `UnspecifiedMap` if the map has not been created yet

**KeySize() uint32**
- Returns the size in bytes of keys for this map

**ValueSize() uint32**
- Returns the size in bytes of values for this map

**MaxEntries() uint32**
- Returns the maximum number of entries the map can hold

**Flags() uint32**
- Returns the map flags

**FD() int**
- Returns the file descriptor of the underlying eBPF map
- Only valid after the map has been opened/created
